					<h1 id="section_0">Chevron Corporation</h1>

				<div class="minerva__subtitle"><span class="mw-redirectedfrom">&#160;&#160;(Redirected from <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corp.&amp;redirect=no" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevron Corp.">Chevron Corp.</a>)</span></div>

			<div id="bodyContent" class="content"><div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><script>function mfTempOpenSection(id){var block=document.getElementById("mf-section-"+id);block.className+=" open-block";block.previousSibling.className+=" open-block";}</script><div class="mw-parser-output"><section class="mf-section-0" id="mf-section-0">
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">This article is about the oil company mostly in the Americas. For similarly named companies, see <a href="/wiki/Chevron_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Chevron (disambiguation)">Chevron</a>.</div>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Not to be confused with <a href="/wiki/Chevrolet" title="Chevrolet">Chevrolet</a>.</div>
<table class="box-Update plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Update" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article's <b><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">factual accuracy</a> may be compromised due to out-of-date information</b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please update this article to reflect recent events or newly available information.</span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">April 2019</span>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="mw-empty-elt">

</p>
<p><b>Chevron Corporation</b> is an American multinational <a href="/wiki/List_of_oil_exploration_and_production_companies" title="List of oil exploration and production companies">energy corporation</a>. One of the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil#Successor_companies" title="Standard Oil">successor companies</a> of <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a>, it is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/San_Ramon,_California" title="San Ramon, California">San Ramon, California</a>, and active in more than 180 countries. Chevron is engaged in every aspect of the <a href="/wiki/Petroleum" title="Petroleum">oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Natural_gas" title="Natural gas">natural gas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">geothermal energy</a> industries, including <a href="/wiki/Hydrocarbon_exploration" title="Hydrocarbon exploration">hydrocarbon exploration</a> and <a href="/wiki/Petroleum#Extraction" title="Petroleum">production</a>; <a href="/wiki/Refining" title="Refining">refining</a>, marketing and transport; chemicals manufacturing and sales; and <a href="/wiki/Power_generation" class="mw-redirect" title="Power generation">power generation</a>. Chevron is one of the world's largest oil companies; as of 2019<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup>, it ranked eleventh in the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> list of the top US <a href="/wiki/Joint-stock_company#Closely_held_corporations_and_publicly_traded_corporations" title="Joint-stock company">closely held and public corporations</a> and 28th on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_Global_500" title="Fortune Global 500">Fortune Global 500</a> list of the top 500 corporations worldwide.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> It was also one of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Sisters_(oil_companies)" title="Seven Sisters (oil companies)">Seven Sisters</a> that dominated the global petroleum industry from the mid-1940s to the 1970s. Chevron is incorporated in California.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p><table class="infobox vcard" style="width:22em"><caption class="fn org">Chevron href="#cite_note-10-K-4">[4]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><span class="nowrap"><a href="/wiki/Equity_(finance)" title="Equity (finance)">Total equity</a></span></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><img alt="Increase" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/11px-Increase2.svg.png" decoding="async" title="Increase" width="11" height="11" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/17px-Increase2.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b0/Increase2.svg/22px-Increase2.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="300" data-file-height="300"> <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$154.5 billion</span> <span style="font-size:85%;">(2018)</span><sup id="cite_ref-10-K_4-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K-4">[4]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><div style="padding:0.1em 0;line-height:1.2em;">Number of employees</div></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;">~51,900 <span style="font-size:85%;">(December 2018)</span><sup id="cite_ref-10-K_4-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10-K-4">[4]</a></sup></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Subsidiary" title="Subsidiary">Subsidiaries</a></th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><div class="plainlist"><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Texaco" title="Texaco">Texaco</a></li><li><a href="/wiki/Caltex" title="Caltex">Caltex</a></li></ul></div></td></tr><tr><th scope="row" style="padding-right: 0.5em;">Website</th><td style="line-height: 1.35em;"><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.chevron.com">www<wbr></wbr>.chevron<wbr></wbr>.com</a></span> <small>(corporate)</small><br><span class="url"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.chevronwithtechron.com/">ChevronWithTechron.com</a></span> <small>(consumer)</small></td></tr></tbody></table><p>Chevron's downstream operations manufacture and sell products such as fuels, lubricants, additives and petrochemicals. The company's most significant areas of operations are the west coast of North America, the U.S. Gulf Coast, Southeast Asia, South Korea and Australia. In 2018, the company produced an average of 791,000 barrels of net oil-equivalent per day in United States.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup></p>

</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(1)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History" data-section="1" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-1 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-1">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Predecessors">Predecessors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Predecessors" data-section="2" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Oil.svg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/220px-Big_Oil.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="211" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="720"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 211px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/220px-Big_Oil.svg.png" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="211" data-srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/330px-Big_Oil.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/89/Big_Oil.svg/440px-Big_Oil.svg.png 2x" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Big_Oil.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chart of the major <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">energy</a> companies dubbed "Big Oil" sorted by latest published revenue</div></div></div>
<p>One of Chevron's early predecessors, <b>Star Oil</b>, discovered oil at the <a href="/wiki/Pico_Canyon_Oilfield" title="Pico Canyon Oilfield">Pico Canyon Oilfield</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Santa_Susana_Mountains" title="Santa Susana Mountains">Santa Susana Mountains</a> north of Los Angeles in 1876. The 25 barrels of oil per day well marked the discovery of the Newhall Field, and is considered by geophysicist <a href="/wiki/Marius_Vassiliou" title="Marius Vassiliou">Marius Vassiliou</a> as the beginning of the modern oil industry in California.<sup id="cite_ref-Vassiliou2009_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vassiliou2009-9">[9]</a></sup> Energy analyst <a href="/wiki/Antonia_Juhasz" title="Antonia Juhasz">Antonia Juhasz</a> has said that while Star Oil's founders were influential in establishing an oil industry in California, Union Mattole Company discovered oil in the state eleven years prior.<sup id="cite_ref-Juhasz2009_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juhasz2009-10">[10]</a></sup></p><p>In September 1879, <a href="/wiki/Charles_N._Felton" title="Charles N. Felton">Charles N. Felton</a>, Lloyd Tevis, George Loomis and others created the <b>Pacific Coast Oil Company</b>, which acquired the assets of Star Oil<sup id="cite_ref-Vassiliou2009_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vassiliou2009-9">[9]</a></sup> with $1 million in funding.<sup id="cite_ref-Karliner1997_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karliner1997-11">[11]</a></sup> Pacific Coast Oil became the largest oil interest in California <sup id="cite_ref-Karliner1997_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Karliner1997-11">[11]</a></sup> by the time it was acquired by <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a> for $761,000 in 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-Vassiliou2009_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Vassiliou2009-9">[9]</a></sup> Pacific Coast operated independently and retained its name until 1906, when it was merged with a Standard Oil subsidiary and it became <b>Standard Oil Company</b> (California) or <b>California Standard</b>.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-12">[12]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Falola2005_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falola2005-13">[13]</a></sup></p><p>Another predecessor, Texas Fuel Company, was founded in 1901, in <a href="/wiki/Beaumont,_Texas" title="Beaumont, Texas">Beaumont, Texas</a> as an oil equipment vendor by "Buckskin Joe". The founder's nickname came from being harsh and aggressive.<sup id="cite_ref-Juhasz2009_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Juhasz2009-10">[10]</a></sup> Texas Fuel worked closely with Chevron. In 1936, it formed a joint venture with California Standard named <a href="/wiki/Caltex" title="Caltex">Caltex</a>, to drill and produce oil in <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-HallRamírez-Pascualli2012_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HallRam%C3%ADrez-Pascualli2012-14">[14]</a></sup> According to energy analyst and activist shareholder <a href="/wiki/Antonia_Juhasz" title="Antonia Juhasz">Antonia Juhasz</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-huffington280910_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-huffington280910-15">[15]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj290910_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj290910-16">[16]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ens140411_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ens140411-17">[17]</a></sup>  the Texas Fuel Company and California Standard were often referred to as the "terrible twins" for their cutthroat business practices.<sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-18">[18]</a></sup> The Texas Fuel Company was renamed the Texas Company, and later renamed <a href="/wiki/Texaco" title="Texaco">Texaco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Falola2005_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Falola2005-13">[13]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Formation_of_the_Chevron_name">Formation of the Chevron name</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Formation of the Chevron name" data-section="3" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Standardgasstation.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Standardgasstation.jpg/220px-Standardgasstation.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Standardgasstation.jpg/220px-Standardgasstation.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Standardgasstation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Chevron station branded under the Standard name in <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_metropolitan_area" class="mw-redirect" title="Las Vegas metropolitan area">Las Vegas</a></div></div></div>
<p>In 1911, the federal government broke Standard Oil into several pieces under the <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Antitrust_Act" class="mw-redirect" title="Sherman Antitrust Act">Sherman Antitrust Act</a>. One of those pieces, Standard Oil Co. (California), went on to become Chevron. It became part of the "<a href="/wiki/Seven_Sisters_(oil_companies)" title="Seven Sisters (oil companies)">Seven Sisters</a>", which dominated the world oil industry in the early 20th century. In 1926, the company changed its name to Standard Oil Co. of California (SOCAL).<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> By the terms of the breakup of Standard Oil, at first Standard of California could use the Standard name only within its original geographic area of the Pacific coast states, plus Nevada and Arizona; outside that area, it had to use another name. Today Chevron is the owner of the <a href="/wiki/Standard_Oil" title="Standard Oil">Standard Oil</a> trademark in 16 states in the western and southeastern U.S. To maintain ownership of the mark, the company owns and operates one Standard-branded Chevron station in each state of the area,<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> although its status in Kentucky is unclear after Chevron withdrew retail sales from Kentucky in July 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p><p>The Chevron name came into use for some of its retail products in the 1930s. The name <b>Calso</b> was also used from 1946 to 1955, in states outside its native West Coast territory.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup></p><p>Standard Oil Company of California ranked 75th among United States corporations in the value of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> military production contracts.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p><p>In 1933, <a href="/wiki/Saudi_Arabia" title="Saudi Arabia">Saudi Arabia</a> granted California Standard a concession to find oil, which led to the discovery of oil in 1938. In 1948, California Standard discovered the world's largest oil field in Saudi Arabia, <a href="/wiki/Ghawar_Field" title="Ghawar Field">Ghawar Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> California Standard's subsidiary, California-Arabian Standard Oil Company, grew over the years and became the Arabian American Oil Company (ARAMCO) in 1944. In 1973, the Saudi government began buying into ARAMCO. By 1980, the company was entirely owned by the Saudis, and in 1988, its name was changed to Saudi Arabian Oil Company—<a href="/wiki/Saudi_Aramco" title="Saudi Aramco">Saudi Aramco</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup></p><p>Standard Oil of California and <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Oil" title="Gulf Oil">Gulf Oil</a> merged in 1984, which was the largest merger in history at that time. To comply with <a href="/wiki/U.S._antitrust_law" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S. antitrust law">U.S. antitrust law</a>, California Standard divested many of Gulf's operating subsidiaries, and sold some Gulf stations and a refinery in the eastern United States. (The refinery is currently owned by <a href="/wiki/Sunoco" class="mw-redirect" title="Sunoco">Sunoco</a>.) Among the assets sold off were Gulf's retail outlets in Gulf's home market of <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, where Chevron lacks a retail presence but does retain a regional headquarters there as of 2013, partially for <a href="/wiki/Marcellus_Formation" title="Marcellus Formation">Marcellus Shale</a>-related drilling.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The same year, Standard Oil of California also took the opportunity to change its legal name to <b>Chevron Corporation</b>, since it had already been using the well-known "Chevron" retail brand name for decades. Chevron would sell the Gulf Oil trademarks for the entire U.S. to <a href="/wiki/Cumberland_Farms" title="Cumberland Farms">Cumberland Farms</a>, the parent company of <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Oil_LP" title="Gulf Oil LP">Gulf Oil LP</a>, in 2010 after Cumberland Farms had a license to the Gulf trademark in the <a href="/wiki/Northeastern_United_States" title="Northeastern United States">Northeastern United States</a> since 1986.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p><p>In 1996 Chevron transferred its natural gas gathering, operating and marketing operation to <a href="/wiki/Dynegy" title="Dynegy">NGC Corporation</a> (later Dynegy) in exchange for a roughly 25% equity stake in NGC.<sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-Nov-1996-10-Q_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-Nov-1996-10-Q-29">[29]</a></sup>  In a merger completed February 1, 2000, Illinova Corp. became a wholly owned subsidiary of Dynegy Inc. and Chevron's stake increased up to 28%.<sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-Mar-2000-8-K_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-Mar-2000-8-K-30">[30]</a></sup> However, in May 2007, Chevron sold its stake in the company for approximately $985 million, resulting in a gain of $680 million.<sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-May-2007-8-K_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-May-2007-8-K-31">[31]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Merger_with_Texaco_and_post-merger">Merger with Texaco and post-merger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Merger with Texaco and post-merger" data-section="4" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On October 10, 2000, Texaco announced the purchase of <a href="/wiki/General_Motors" title="General Motors">General Motors</a>' share in GM Ovonics<sup id="cite_ref-cobasys1_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cobasys1-33">[33]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-autonews_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-autonews-34">[34]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-evuk_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-evuk-35">[35]</a></sup>, a manufacturer of <a href="/wiki/Nickel%E2%80%93metal_hydride_battery" title="Nickel–metal hydride battery">NiMH batteries</a> for electric cars, which in 2003, was restructured into <a href="/wiki/Cobasys" title="Cobasys">Cobasys</a>, a 50/50 joint venture between Chevron and <a href="/wiki/Energy_Conversion_Devices_Ovonics" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy Conversion Devices Ovonics">Energy Conversion Devices Ovonics</a>. In 2009, both Chevron and Energy Conservation Devices sold their stakes in Cobasys to SB LiMotive Co.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>On October 15, 2000, Chevron announced acquisition of <a href="/wiki/Texaco" title="Texaco">Texaco</a> in a deal valued at $45 billion, creating the second-largest oil company in the United States and the world's fourth-largest publicly traded oil company with a combined market value of approximately $95 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-Oct-2000-8-K_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-Oct-2000-8-K-36">[36]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> The acquisition was completed on October 9, 2001.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup> The merged company was named <b>ChevronTexaco</b>. On May 9, 2005, ChevronTexaco announced it would drop the Texaco <a href="/wiki/Moniker" class="mw-redirect" title="Moniker">moniker</a> and return to the Chevron name. Texaco remained as a brand under the Chevron Corporation.<sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-May-2005-8-K_41-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-May-2005-8-K-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrongasstation.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Chevrongasstation.jpg/220px-Chevrongasstation.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="140" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="444"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 140px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Chevrongasstation.jpg/220px-Chevrongasstation.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="140" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chevrongasstation.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chevron gas station design used until 2006</div></div></div>
<p>In 2005, Chevron purchased <a href="/wiki/Unocal_Corporation" title="Unocal Corporation">Unocal Corporation</a> for $18.4 billion, increasing the company's petroleum and natural gas reserves by about 15%.<sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-Apr-2005-8-K_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-Apr-2005-8-K-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-Aug-2005-8-K_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-Aug-2005-8-K-43">[43]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Because of Unocal's large South East Asian geothermal operations, Chevron became a large producer of <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">geothermal energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc190206_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc190206-46">[46]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron and the <a href="/wiki/Los_Alamos_National_Laboratory" title="Los Alamos National Laboratory">Los Alamos National Laboratory</a> started a cooperation in 2006, to improve the recovery of hydrocarbons from <a href="/wiki/Oil_shale" title="Oil shale">oil shale</a> by developing a <a href="/wiki/Shale_oil_extraction" title="Shale oil extraction">shale oil extraction</a> process named <a href="/wiki/Chevron_CRUSH" title="Chevron CRUSH">Chevron CRUSH</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-gcc_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gcc-47">[47]</a></sup>  In 2006, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_the_Interior" title="United States Department of the Interior">United States Department of the Interior</a> issued a research, development and demonstration lease for Chevron's demonstration oil shale project on public lands in Colorado's <a href="/wiki/Piceance_Basin" title="Piceance Basin">Piceance Basin</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-blm_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-blm-48">[48]</a></sup>  In February 2012, Chevron notified the <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_Land_Management" title="Bureau of Land Management">Bureau of Land Management</a> and the Department of Reclamation, Mining and Safety that it intends to divest this lease.<sup id="cite_ref-bizjournals280212_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bizjournals280212-49">[49]</a></sup></p><p>In July 2010, Chevron ended retail operations in the Mid-Atlantic United States, removing the Chevron and Texaco names from 1,100 stations.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>  In 2011, Chevron acquired Pennsylvania based <a href="/wiki/Atlas_Energy_Inc" class="mw-redirect" title="Atlas Energy Inc">Atlas Energy Inc</a>. for $3.2 billion in cash and an additional $1.1 billion in existing debt owed by Atlas.<sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-Nov-2010-DFAN14A_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-Nov-2010-DFAN14A-51">[51]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chevron-Corp-Feb-2011-10-K_53-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron-Corp-Feb-2011-10-K-53">[53]</a></sup>  Three months later, Chevron acquired drilling and development rights for another 228,000 acres in the Marcellus Shale from Chief Oil &amp; Gas LLC and Tug Hill, Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2013, <a href="/wiki/Total_S.A." title="Total S.A.">Total S.A.</a> and its joint venture partner agreed to buy Chevron's retail distribution business in <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a> for an undisclosed amount.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> In October 2014, Chevron announced that it would sell a 30 percent holding in its <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canadian</a> oil shale holdings to <a href="/wiki/Kuwait" title="Kuwait">Kuwait</a>'s state-owned oil company <a href="/wiki/Kuwait_Oil_Company" title="Kuwait Oil Company">Kuwait Oil Company</a> for a fee of $1.5 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup></p><p>In 2016, Chevron announced to exit South Africa, where it has had a presence for over a century.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2019, Chevron announced their intention to acquire Anadarko Petroleum in a deal valued at $33 billion, but decided to focus on other acquisitions shortly afterwards when a deal could not be reached.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p><p>In February 2020, Chevron joins Marubeni Corporation and WAVE Equity Partners in investing in Carbon Clean Solutions, a company that provides portable carbon capture technology for the oil field and other industrial facilities.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(2)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Operations">Operations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Operations" data-section="5" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-2 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-2">
<p>As of December 31, 2018, Chevron had approximately 48,600 employees (including about 3,600 service station employees). Approximately 24,800 employees (including about 3,300 service station employees), or 51 percent, were employed in U.S. operations.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2015, Chevron announced that it is cutting up to 7,000 jobs, or 11 percent of its workforce.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Upstream">Upstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Upstream" data-section="6" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Chevron's oil and gas exploration and production operations are primarily in the US, Australia, Nigeria, Angola, Kazakhstan, and the Gulf of Mexico.  As of December 31, 2018, the company's upstream business reported worldwide net production of 2.930 million oil-equivalent barrels per day.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ChevronInWyoming.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/ChevronInWyoming.jpg/220px-ChevronInWyoming.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="128" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3197" data-file-height="1859"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 128px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/ChevronInWyoming.jpg/220px-ChevronInWyoming.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="128" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ChevronInWyoming.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Chevron gas station in <a href="/wiki/Diamondville,_Wyoming" title="Diamondville, Wyoming">Diamondville, Wyoming</a> (taken on May 27, 2018).</div></div></div>
<p>In the United States, the company operates approximately 11,000 oil and natural gas wells in hundreds of fields occupying 4,000,000 acres (16,000 km<sup>2</sup>) across the <a href="/wiki/Permian_Basin_(North_America)" title="Permian Basin (North America)">Permian Basin</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/West_Texas" title="West Texas">West Texas</a> and southeastern <a href="/wiki/New_Mexico" title="New Mexico">New Mexico</a>. In 2010, Chevron was the fourth largest producer in the region.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> In February 2011, Chevron celebrated the production of its 5 billionth barrel of Permian Basin oil.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> The Gulf of Mexico is where the company's deepest offshore drilling takes place at Tahiti and Blind Faith. It also explores and drills the <a href="/wiki/Marcellus_Shale" class="mw-redirect" title="Marcellus Shale">Marcellus Shale</a> formation under several northeastern US states.
</p><p>Chevron's largest single resource project is the $43 billion <a href="/wiki/Gorgon_Gas_Project" class="mw-redirect" title="Gorgon Gas Project">Gorgon Gas Project</a> in Australia. It also produces natural gas from Western Australia.  The $43 billion project was started in 2010, and was expected to be brought online in 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> The project includes construction of a 15 million tonne per annum <a href="/wiki/Liquefied_natural_gas_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Liquefied natural gas plant">liquefied natural gas plant</a> on <a href="/wiki/Barrow_Island_(Western_Australia)" title="Barrow Island (Western Australia)">Barrow Island</a>, and a domestic gas plant with the capacity to provide 300 terajoules per day to supply gas to Western Australia.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup> It is also developing the <a href="/wiki/Wheatstone_LNG" title="Wheatstone LNG">Wheatstone liquefied natural gas development</a> in Western Australia. The foundation phase of the project is estimated to cost $29 billion; it will consist of two LNG processing trains with a combined capacity of 8.9 million tons per annum, a domestic gas plant and associated offshore infrastructure.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> In August 2014 a significant gas-condensate discovery at the Lasseter-1 exploration well in WA-274-P in Western Australia, in which Chevron has a 50% interest was announced.<sup id="cite_ref-SantosWA_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SantosWA-68">[68]</a></sup> The company also has an interest in the <a href="/wiki/North_West_Shelf_Venture" title="North West Shelf Venture">North West Shelf Venture</a>, equally shared with five other investors including <a href="/wiki/BP" title="BP">BP</a>, <a href="/wiki/BHP" title="BHP">BHP Billiton Petroleum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shell_Australia" title="Shell Australia">Shell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mitsubishi" title="Mitsubishi">Mitsubishi</a>/<a href="/wiki/Mitsui" title="Mitsui">Mitsui</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodside_Petroleum" title="Woodside Petroleum">Woodside</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p><p>In the onshore and near-offshore regions of the <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta" title="Niger Delta">Niger Delta</a>, Chevron operates under a joint venture with the <a href="/wiki/Nigerian_National_Petroleum_Corporation" title="Nigerian National Petroleum Corporation">Nigerian National Petroleum Corporation</a>, operating and holding a 40% interest in 13 concessions in the region. In addition, Chevron operates the Escravos Gas Plant and the <a href="/wiki/Escravos_GTL" title="Escravos GTL">Escravos gas-to-liquids plant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron has interests in four concessions in Angola, including offshore two concessions in <a href="/wiki/Cabinda_province" class="mw-redirect" title="Cabinda province">Cabinda province</a>, the Tombua–Landana development and the Mafumeira Norte project, operated by the company.  It is also a leading partner in <a href="/wiki/Angola_LNG_plant" class="mw-redirect" title="Angola LNG plant">Angola LNG plant</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-angola-today.com_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-angola-today.com-72">[72]</a></sup></p><p>In Kazakhstan, Chevron participate the <a href="/wiki/Tengiz_Field" title="Tengiz Field">Tengiz</a> and <a href="/wiki/Karachaganak_Field" title="Karachaganak Field">Karachaganak</a> projects.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup>  In 2010, Chevron became the largest private shareholder in the <a href="/wiki/Caspian_Pipeline_Consortium" title="Caspian Pipeline Consortium">Caspian Pipeline Consortium</a> pipeline, which transports oil from the Caspian Sea to the Black Sea.<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p><p>As of 2013, the <a href="/wiki/Rosebank_oil_and_gas_field" title="Rosebank oil and gas field">Rosebank oil and gas field</a> west of <a href="/wiki/Shetland" title="Shetland">Shetland</a> was being evaluated by Chevron and its partners. Chevron drilled its discovery well there in 2004. Production is expected in 2015 if a decision is made to produce from the field. The geology and weather conditions are challenging.<sup id="cite_ref-NYT72313_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT72313-75">[75]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Midstream">Midstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Midstream" data-section="7" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>As of 2019, Chevron did not own significant <a href="/wiki/Midstream" title="Midstream">midstream</a> assets;<sup id="cite_ref-:0_76-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-76">[76]</a></sup> that year it attempted to purchase <a href="/wiki/Anadarko_Petroleum" title="Anadarko Petroleum">Anadarko Petroleum</a>, which owned pipelines,<sup id="cite_ref-:0_76-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-76">[76]</a></sup> but was outbid by <a href="/wiki/Occidental_Petroleum" title="Occidental Petroleum">Occidental Petroleum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Downstream">Downstream</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Downstream" data-section="8" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Chevron's downstream operations manufacture and sell products such as fuels, lubricants, additives and petrochemicals. The company's most significant areas of operations are the west coast of North America, the U.S. Gulf Coast, Southeast Asia, South Korea, Australia and South Africa.  In 2010, Chevron sold an average of 3.1 million barrels per day (490<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>3</sup> m<sup>3</sup>/d) of refined products like gasoline, diesel and jet fuel.<sup id="cite_ref-sec-refining_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-refining-78">[78]</a></sup>  The company operates approximately 19,550 retail sites in 84 countries. The company also has interests in 13 power generating assets in the United States and Asia and has gas stations in <a href="/wiki/Western_Canada" title="Western Canada">Western Canada</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Chevron owns the trademark rights to Texaco and Caltex fuel and lubricant products.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>In 2010, Chevron processed 1.9 million barrels per day (300<span style="margin-left:0.2em">×<span style="margin-left:0.1em">10</span></span><s style="display:none">^</s><sup>3</sup> m<sup>3</sup>/d) of crude oil.<sup id="cite_ref-sec-refining_78-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sec-refining-78">[78]</a></sup>  It owns and operates Five active refineries in the United States (<a href="/wiki/Richmond,_CA" class="mw-redirect" title="Richmond, CA">Richmond, CA</a>, <a href="/wiki/El_Segundo,_CA" class="mw-redirect" title="El Segundo, CA">El Segundo, CA</a>,<a href="/wiki/Salt_Lake_City,_UT" class="mw-redirect" title="Salt Lake City, UT">Salt Lake City, UT</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pascagoula,_MS" class="mw-redirect" title="Pascagoula, MS">Pascagoula, MS</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pasadena,_TX" class="mw-redirect" title="Pasadena, TX">Pasadena, TX</a> ). Chevron is the non-operating partner in seven joint venture refineries, located in Australia,<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Pakistan" title="Pakistan">Pakistan</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">Singapore</a>, <a href="/wiki/Thailand" title="Thailand">Thailand</a>, South Korea, and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> Chevron's United States refineries are located in Gulf and Western states. Chevron also owns an asphalt refinery in Perth Amboy, New Jersey; however, since early 2008 that refinery has primarily operated as a terminal.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron's chemicals business includes 50% ownership in the <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Phillips" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevron Phillips">Chevron Phillips</a> Chemical Company, which manufactures petrochemicals, and the Chevron Oronite Company (which develops, manufactures and sells fuel and lubricant additives).<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron Chemical produced <a href="/wiki/Paraquat" title="Paraquat">paraquat</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron Shipping Company, a wholly owned subsidiary, provides the maritime transport operations, marine consulting services and marine risk management services for Chevron Corporation.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Chevron ships historically had names beginning with "Chevron", such as <i>Chevron Washington</i> and <i>Chevron South America</i>, or were named after former or serving directors of the company. <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Ginn" title="Samuel Ginn">Samuel Ginn</a>, William E. Crain, <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Derr" class="mw-redirect" title="Kenneth Derr">Kenneth Derr</a>, Richard Matzke and most notably <a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> were among those honored, but the ship named after Rice was subsequently renamed as <i>Altair Voyager</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Alternative_energy">Alternative energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Alternative energy" data-section="9" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solarmine1.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Solarmine1.jpg/220px-Solarmine1.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3236" data-file-height="2310"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 157px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Solarmine1.jpg/220px-Solarmine1.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="157" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solarmine1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chevron's 500kW Solarmine <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic_array" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic array">photovoltaic</a> solar project in <a href="/wiki/Fellows,_California" title="Fellows, California">Fellows, California</a></div></div></div>
<p>Chevron's alternative energy operations include geothermal <a href="/wiki/Solar_energy" title="Solar energy">solar</a>, wind, <a href="/wiki/Biofuel" title="Biofuel">biofuel</a>, fuel cells, and <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-latimes220310_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-latimes220310-86">[86]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron has claimed to be the world's largest producer of <a href="/wiki/Geothermal_energy" title="Geothermal energy">geothermal energy</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc190206_46-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc190206-46">[46]</a></sup>  The company's primary geothermal operations were located in Southeast Asia, but these assets were sold in 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-bloomberg070711_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bloomberg070711-87">[87]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup></p><p>Prior, Chevron operated geothermal wells in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> providing power to Jakarta and the surrounding area. In the <a href="/wiki/Philippines" title="Philippines">Philippines</a>, Chevron also operated geothermal wells at Tiwi field in Albay province, the Makiling-Banahaw field in Laguna and Quezon provinces.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup></p><p>In 2007, Chevron and the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Energy" title="United States Department of Energy">United States Department of Energy</a>'s <a href="/wiki/National_Renewable_Energy_Laboratory" title="National Renewable Energy Laboratory">National Renewable Energy Laboratory</a> (NREL) started collaboration to develop and produce <a href="/wiki/Algae_fuel" title="Algae fuel">algae fuel</a>, which could be converted into transportation fuels, such as <a href="/wiki/Jet_fuel" title="Jet fuel">jet fuel</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup>  In 2008, Chevron and <a href="/wiki/Weyerhaeuser" title="Weyerhaeuser">Weyerhaeuser</a> created Catchlight Energy LLC, which researches the conversion of cellulose-based biomass into biofuels.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup>  In 2013, the Catchlight plan was downsized due to competition with fossil fuel projects for funds.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p><p>Between 2006 and 2011, Chevron contributed up to $12 million to a strategic research alliance with the Georgia Institute of Technology to develop cellulosic biofuels and to create a process to convert biomass like wood or switchgrass into fuels.
Additionally, Chevron holds a 22% stake in Galveston Bay Biodiesel LP, which produces up to 110 million US gallons (420,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of renewable biodiesel fuel a year.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup></p><p>In 2010, the Chevron announced a 740 kW <a href="/wiki/Photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Photovoltaic">photovoltaic</a> demonstration project in <a href="/wiki/Bakersfield,_California" title="Bakersfield, California">Bakersfield, California</a>, called Project Brightfield, for exploring possibilities to use <a href="/wiki/Solar_power" title="Solar power">solar power</a> for powering Chevron's facilities. It consists of technologies from seven companies, which Chevron is evaluating for large-scale use.<sup id="cite_ref-ustoday260511_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ustoday260511-97">[97]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt220510_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt220510-98">[98]</a></sup>  In <a href="/wiki/Fellows,_California" title="Fellows, California">Fellows, California</a>, Chevron has invested in the 500 kW Solarmine photovoltaic solar project, which supplies daytime power to the <a href="/wiki/Midway-Sunset_Oil_Field" title="Midway-Sunset Oil Field">Midway-Sunset Oil Field</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-ogj220510_99-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ogj220510-99">[99]</a></sup>  In Questa, Chevron has built a 1 MW <a href="/wiki/Concentrated_photovoltaic" class="mw-redirect" title="Concentrated photovoltaic">concentrated photovoltaic</a> plant that comprises 173 solar arrays, which use <a href="/wiki/Fresnel_lens" title="Fresnel lens">Fresnel lenses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup>  In October 2011, Chevron launched a 29-MW <a href="/wiki/Solar_thermal_energy" title="Solar thermal energy">thermal solar-to-steam facility</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Coalinga_Field" class="mw-redirect" title="Coalinga Field">Coalinga Field</a> to produce the steam for <a href="/wiki/Enhanced_oil_recovery" title="Enhanced oil recovery">enhanced oil recovery</a>. As of 2012, the project is the largest of its kind in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup></p><p>In 2014, Chevron began reducing its investment in renewable energy technologies, reducing headcount and selling alternative energy-related assets.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup></p><p>In 2015, the <a href="/wiki/Shell_Canada" title="Shell Canada">Shell Canada</a> Quest Energy project was launched<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_104-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada-104">[104]</a></sup> of which Chevron Canada Limited holds a 20% share.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> The project is based within the Athabasca Oil Sands Project near Fort McMurray, Alberta. It is the world's first <a href="/wiki/Carbon_capture_and_storage" title="Carbon capture and storage">CCS</a> project on a commercial-scale.<sup id="cite_ref-Canada_104-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Canada-104">[104]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(3)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs">Corporate affairs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs" data-section="10" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-3 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-3">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Finance">Finance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Finance" data-section="11" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>For the fiscal year 2011, Chevron reported earnings of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>26.9 billion, with an annual revenue of <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>257.3 billion, an increase of 23.3% over the previous fiscal cycle. Chevron's shares traded at over $105 per share, and its market capitalization was valued at over <span style="white-space: nowrap">US$</span>240 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-cbsnews_106-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cbsnews-106">[106]</a></sup> As of 2018, Chevron is ranked #13 on the <a href="/wiki/Fortune_500" title="Fortune 500">Fortune 500</a> rankings of the largest United States corporations by total revenue.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup></p>

</td></tr></tbody></table><h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Headquarters">Headquarters</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Headquarters" data-section="12" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Houston1.JPG" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Downtown_Houston1.JPG/220px-Downtown_Houston1.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="1280"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 293px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Downtown_Houston1.JPG/220px-Downtown_Houston1.JPG" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="293" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Downtown_Houston1.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Chevron tower in Houston</div></div></div>
<p>Chevron's corporate headquarters are located in a 92-acre campus in <a href="/wiki/San_Ramon,_California" title="San Ramon, California">San Ramon, California</a>. The company moved there in 2002 from its earlier headquarters at <a href="/wiki/555_Market_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="555 Market Street">555 Market Street</a> in <a href="/wiki/San_Francisco,_California" class="mw-redirect" title="San Francisco, California">San Francisco, California</a>, the city where it had been located since its inception in 1879.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> Chevron also operates from office towers in <a href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" class="mw-redirect" title="Houston, Texas">Houston, Texas</a>, where it purchased <a href="/wiki/1500_Louisiana_Street" title="1500 Louisiana Street">1500 Louisiana Street</a> and <a href="/wiki/1400_Smith_Street" title="1400 Smith Street">1400 Smith Street</a> from former Texas energy giant <a href="/wiki/Enron" title="Enron">Enron</a>. Chevron is also planning a new office tower in downtown Houston next to its existing properties at <a href="/w/index.php?title=1600_Louisiana_Street&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="1600 Louisiana Street (page does not exist)">1600 Louisiana Street</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-houstbiz_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-houstbiz-111">[111]</a></sup> The building will stand 50-stories and 832 feet. Upon completion, it will be the fourth tallest building in Houston and the first 50-story building constructed there in nearly 30 years.
</p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Political_contributions">Political contributions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Political contributions" data-section="13" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Since January 2011 Chevron has contributed almost $15 million on Washington lobbying. On October 7, 2012 Chevron donated $2.5 million to the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican</a> <a href="/wiki/Congressional_Leadership_Fund" title="Congressional Leadership Fund">Congressional Leadership Fund</a> super <a href="/wiki/Political_action_committee" title="Political action committee">PAC</a> that is closely tied to former <a href="/wiki/Speaker_of_the_United_States_House_of_Representatives" title="Speaker of the United States House of Representatives">House Speaker</a> <a href="/wiki/John_Boehner" title="John Boehner">John Boehner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Board_of_directors">Board of directors</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Board of directors" data-section="14" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Wirth" title="Michael Wirth">Michael Wirth</a> (Chairman &amp; CEO)</li>
<li><a href="/w/index.php?title=Debra_Reed-Klages&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Debra Reed-Klages (page does not exist)">Debra Reed-Klages</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Inge_Thulin" title="Inge Thulin">Inge Thulin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Enrique_Hernandez,_Jr." class="mw-redirect" title="Enrique Hernandez, Jr.">Enrique Hernandez, Jr.</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Alice_P._Gast" class="mw-redirect" title="Alice P. Gast">Alice P. Gast</a></li>
