<li><a href="/wiki/Ronald_Sugar" title="Ronald Sugar">Ronald Sugar</a> Lead Director</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Wanda_Austin" title="Wanda Austin">Wanda Austin</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dambisa_Moyo" title="Dambisa Moyo">Dambisa Moyo</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jim_Umpleby" title="Jim Umpleby">Jim Umpleby</a></li></ul><p><a href="/wiki/Condoleezza_Rice" title="Condoleezza Rice">Condoleezza Rice</a> is a former member of the board of directors, and also headed Chevron's committee on public policy until she resigned on January 15, 2001, to become National Security Advisor to President George W. Bush.
</p><p>On September 30, 2009, John Watson, age 52, was elected Chairman of the Board and CEO, effective at the December 31, 2009 retirement of <a href="/wiki/David_J._O%27Reilly" title="David J. O'Reilly">David J. O'Reilly</a>.
</p><p>In September 2017, Chevron announced Watson would retire on February 1, 2018 and Vice Chairman Mike Wirth would be elevated to the role of chairman &amp; CEO.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(4)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Niger_Delta_Partnership_Initiative">Niger Delta Partnership Initiative</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Niger Delta Partnership Initiative" data-section="15" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-4 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-4">
<p>In 2010 Chevron established the Niger Delta Partnership Initiative (NDPI), a non-profit that works with local
organizations to promote economic growth, reduce HIV transmission rates, and empower women.  The Initiative was initially funded with a $50 million grant.  An additional $40 million was donated in 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> NDPI's work has enabled and strengthened relationships between local individuals and hundreds of organizations, resulting in more than $92 million of new investment into the region in both monetary and in-kind resources since 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup></p>
</section><h2 class="section-heading" onclick="javascript:mfTempOpenSection(5)"><div class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element indicator mw-ui-icon-small mw-ui-icon-flush-left"></div><span class="mw-headline" id="Controversies">Controversies<span id="Environmental_record"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Controversies" data-section="16" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h2><section class="mf-section-5 collapsible-block" id="mf-section-5">
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Environmental_damage_in_Ecuador">Environmental damage in Ecuador</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Environmental damage in Ecuador" data-section="17" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Lago_Agrio_oil_field" title="Lago Agrio oil field">Lago Agrio oil field</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Texaco_in_Ecuador.jpg" class="image"><noscript><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Texaco_in_Ecuador.jpg/220px-Texaco_in_Ecuador.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="3648" data-file-height="2736"></noscript><span class="lazy-image-placeholder" style="width: 220px;height: 165px;" data-src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/eb/Texaco_in_Ecuador.jpg/220px-Texaco_in_Ecuador.jpg" data-alt="" data-width="220" data-height="165" data-class="thumbimage"> </span></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Texaco_in_Ecuador.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Oil pollution in Lago Agrio, November 2007</div></div></div>
<p>Texaco and Gulf Oil began operating in the Oriente region of Ecuador in 1964 as a consortium.<sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> Texaco operated the <a href="/wiki/Lago_Agrio_oil_field" title="Lago Agrio oil field">Lago Agrio oil field</a> from 1972 to 1993 and the Ecuador state oil company continued to operate the same oil fields after Texaco left. In 1993, Texaco was found responsible for dumping billions of gallons of toxic waste and they spent $40m cleaning up the area during the 1990s.  In 1998, the Ecuadorean government signed an agreement with Texaco accepting the clean-up as complete and absolving Texaco of any further responsibility. That same year, an Ecuadorean scientific team took water and soil samples after Texaco left and found petroleum hydrocarbons at unsafe levels in almost half.  The clean up was called "a sham" by critics.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (March 2015)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup><sup id="cite_ref-finally_118-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finally-118">[118]</a></sup></p><p>In 2003, a class action lawsuit against Chevron was filed in Ecuadorian court for $28 billion by indigenous residents, who accused Texaco of making residents ill and damaging forests and rivers by discharging 18 billion US gallons (68,000,000 m<sup>3</sup>) of <a href="/wiki/Produced_water" title="Produced water">formation water</a> into the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_rainforest" title="Amazon rainforest">Amazon rainforest</a> without any <a href="/wiki/Environmental_remediation" title="Environmental remediation">environmental remediation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> Chevron said that the company had completed cleanup of the pollution caused by Texaco, that current pollution was the result of activities of the Ecuadorian oil interests, and that the 1998 agreements with the Ecuadorian Government exempted the company from any liabilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Kraus_124-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kraus-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shareholders_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shareholders-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Shareholders_125-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Shareholders-125">[125]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, Ecuadorian residents were awarded $8.6 billion, based on claims of loss of crops and farm animals as well as increased local cancer rates.<sup id="cite_ref-finally_118-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finally-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chevron_fined_for_Amazon_pollution_by_Ecuador_court_128-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron_fined_for_Amazon_pollution_by_Ecuador_court-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ecuador_court_orders_Chevron_to_pay_$8_bln_-lawyer_129-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ecuador_court_orders_Chevron_to_pay_%248_bln_-lawyer-129">[129]</a></sup> The plaintiffs said this would not be enough to make up for the damage caused by the oil company.<sup id="cite_ref-Ecuador_plaintiffs_say_Chevron_ruling_falls_short_130-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ecuador_plaintiffs_say_Chevron_ruling_falls_short-130">[130]</a></sup> The award was later revised to $19 billion on appeals, which was then appealed again to the Ecuadorean National Court of Justice.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup>  The action has been called the first time that indigenous people have successfully sued a <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational corporation</a> in the country where the pollution took place.<sup id="cite_ref-finally_118-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finally-118">[118]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Chevron_fined_for_Amazon_pollution_by_Ecuador_court_128-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Chevron_fined_for_Amazon_pollution_by_Ecuador_court-128">[128]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Ecuador_plaintiffs_say_Chevron_ruling_falls_short_130-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Ecuador_plaintiffs_say_Chevron_ruling_falls_short-130">[130]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron described the lawsuit as an "extortion scheme" and refused to pay the fine.<sup id="cite_ref-finally_118-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-finally-118">[118]</a></sup></p><p>In November 2013, the international arbitration tribunal issued a partial award in favour of Chevron and its subsidiary, Texaco Petroleum Company. The tribunal has found Chevron is not liable for environmental claims in Ecuador.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p><p>In March 2014, a United States district court judge ruled that the Ecuadorian plaintiff's lead attorney, <a href="/wiki/Steven_Donziger" title="Steven Donziger">Steven Donziger</a>, had used "corrupt means," including "coercion, bribery, money laundering and other misconduct," to obtain the 2011 court verdict in Ecuador. The judge did not rule on the underlying issue of environmental damages. While the US ruling does not affect the decision of the court in Ecuador, it has blocked efforts to collect damages from Chevron in US courts. Donziger has appealed.<sup id="cite_ref-Kraus_124-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kraus-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kraus_124-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kraus-124">[124]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-wsj_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-wsj-133">[133]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p><p>In April 2015, <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Watch" title="Amazon Watch">AmazonWatch</a> released videos reportedly sent from a whistleblower inside Chevron.  The videos purportedly show employees and consultants finding petroleum contamination at sites in the Ecuadorean Amazon that the company claimed was cleaned up years earlier. These videos were confirmed as legitimate by Chevron legal counsel.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup>  According to the company, the videos show routine testing to establish the perimeter of oil pits.  The company further stated that it is not possible to determine from the videos whether the sites shown are the responsibility of Chevron or its former partner, Petroecuador.  According to Amazon Watch, the videos contain a map confirming that the sites are Chevron's, and contain footage of interviews with villagers known to live in the area for which Chevron is responsible.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup></p><p>In September 2018, an international tribunal ruled in  favor of Chevron Corp  finding that Ecuador had violated its obligations under international treaties.  The tribunal held that a $9.5 billion pollution judgment by Ecuador's Supreme Court against Chevron “was procured through fraud, bribery and corruption and was based on claims that had been already settled and released by the Republic of Ecuador years earlier.”  Ecuador's attorney general  plans to appeal the tribunal's ruling saying, “It worries us that the tribunal is asking a country to lift a sentence of one of its courts that was issued as part of a dispute between private parties."<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron continues to take oil from the Amazon region at large. El Segundo (CA), Pascagoula (MS), and Richmond (CA) refineries all process Amazonian oil. In 2015 El Segundo was the single largest refiner in the U.S. of Amazon Crude, processing 54,463 barrels per day.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_spills_in_Angola">Oil spills in Angola</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Oil spills in Angola" data-section="18" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, Chevron's operations in Africa were criticized as environmentally unsound by 130 Nigerian researchers, journalists, and activists.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> In 2002 Angola demanded $2 million in compensation for oil spills allegedly caused by Chevron, the first time it had fined a multinational corporation operating in its waters.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="U.S._Clean_Air_Act_Settlements">U.S. Clean Air Act Settlements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: U.S. Clean Air Act Settlements" data-section="19" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On October 16, 2003, Chevron U.S.A. settled a charge under the <a href="/wiki/Clean_Air_Act_(United_States)" class="mw-redirect" title="Clean Air Act (United States)">Clean Air Act</a>, which reduced harmful air emissions by about 10,000 tons a year.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_Protection_Agency_141-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_Protection_Agency-141">[141]</a></sup> In San Francisco, Chevron was filed by a consent decree to spend almost $275 million to install and utilize innovative technology to reduce nitrogen and sulfur dioxide emissions at its refineries.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> In 2000, Chevron paid a $6 million penalty as well as $1 million for environmental improvement projects to settle charges of Clean Air Act violations related to  offline loading terminal operations in <a href="/wiki/El_Segundo,_California" title="El Segundo, California">El Segundo, California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-justice.gov_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justice.gov-143">[143]</a></sup> Chevron also had implemented programs that minimized production of hazardous gases, upgraded leak detection and repair procedure, reduced emissions from sulfur recovery plants, and adopted strategies to ensure the proper handling of harmful benzene wastes at refineries.<sup id="cite_ref-Environmental_Protection_Agency_141-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Environmental_Protection_Agency-141">[141]</a></sup> Chevron also spent about $500,000 to install leakless valves and double-sealed pumps at its El Segundo refinery, which could prevent significant emissions of air contaminants.<sup id="cite_ref-justice.gov_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-justice.gov-143">[143]</a></sup></p><p>In 2011, Chevron was recognized by the environmental group Ceres for its efforts to reduce <a href="/wiki/Global_warming" title="Global warming">global warming</a> by cutting its own emissions and investing in renewable energy technologies. Soon after, it began reducing its investments in renewables.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="NiMH_battery_technology_for_automobiles">NiMH battery technology for automobiles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: NiMH battery technology for automobiles" data-section="20" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<table class="box-More_citations_needed plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This article <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.<br><small><span class="plainlinks"><i>Find sources:</i> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?as_eq=wikipedia&amp;q=%22Chevron+Corporation%22">"Chevron Corporation"</a> – <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbm=nws&amp;q=%22Chevron+Corporation%22+-wikipedia">news</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?&amp;q=%22Chevron+Corporation%22+site:news.google.com/newspapers&amp;source=newspapers">newspapers</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//www.google.com/search?tbs=bks:1&amp;q=%22Chevron+Corporation%22+-wikipedia">books</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="//scholar.google.com/scholar?q=%22Chevron+Corporation%22">scholar</a> <b>·</b> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.jstor.org/action/doBasicSearch?Query=%22Chevron+Corporation%22&amp;acc=on&amp;wc=on">JSTOR</a></span></small></span>  <small class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2015</span>)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table><p><b>Cobasys LLC</b> was a supplier of <a href="/wiki/Nickel_metal_hydride_battery" class="mw-redirect" title="Nickel metal hydride battery">nickel metal hydride (NiMH)</a> batteries, battery control systems, and packaged solutions for automotive applications, <a href="/wiki/Uninterruptable_power_supply" class="mw-redirect" title="Uninterruptable power supply">uninterruptable power supplies</a>, telecommunications applications, and distributed power generation.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> For 8 years ending in 2009, Cobasys was a 50-50 joint venture between California-based Chevron Corporation and Michigan-based <a href="/wiki/Energy_Conversion_Devices_Ovonics" class="mw-redirect" title="Energy Conversion Devices Ovonics">Energy Conversion Devices, Inc.</a> (also called ECD Ovonics, ECD, or Ovonics)<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-roberson_147-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-roberson-147">[147]</a></sup> The intermediary hierarchy of ownership was that Cobasys LLC was owned by Chevron's subsidiary Chevron Technology Ventures LLC, and ECD Ovonics' subsidiary Ovonic Battery Company.<sup id="cite_ref-ovonicmaterials_148-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ovonicmaterials-148">[148]</a></sup>  Cobasys spent $180 million in funding from Chevron Technology Ventures, and the two owners were unable to agree on further funding of the company.  After arbitration between the owners had stalled, a buyer was found.  On July 14, 2009, the sale of Cobasys to <a href="/wiki/SB_LiMotive" title="SB LiMotive">SB LiMotive Co. Ltd.</a>, an electric vehicle battery joint venture between <a href="/wiki/Samsung" title="Samsung">Samsung SDI Co. Ltd.</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Bosch_GmbH" title="Robert Bosch GmbH">Robert Bosch GmbH</a>, was announced.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Sherry_Boschert" title="Sherry Boschert">Sherry Boschert</a>  accused Chevron of limiting access to large <a href="/wiki/NiMH" class="mw-redirect" title="NiMH">NiMH</a> batteries through its stake in <a href="/wiki/Cobasys" title="Cobasys">Cobasys</a> corporation and control of patent licenses in order to remove a competitor to gasoline.  Cobasys filed a patent infringement lawsuit against <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Toyota" title="Toyota">Toyota</a> over production of the EV-95 battery used in the RAV4 EV.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup>  The case was settled with each company granting the other a license to its patents.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> In her book, <i>Plug-in Hybrids: The Cars that Will Recharge America</i>, published in February 2007, <a href="/wiki/Sherry_Boschert" title="Sherry Boschert">Sherry Boschert</a> argues that large-format NiMH batteries are commercially viable but that Cobasys refuses to sell the batteries or license the technology to small companies or individuals. Boschert argues that Cobasys accepts only very large orders for the batteries. Major automakers showed little interest in placing large orders for large-format NiMH batteries. However, Toyota complained about the difficulty in getting smaller orders of large format NiMH batteries to service the existing 825 RAV-4EVs. Because no other companies were willing to place large orders, Cobasys was not manufacturing or licensing large format NiMH battery technology for automobiles. Boschert concludes that "it's possible that Cobasys (Chevron) is squelching all access to large NiMH batteries through its control of patent licenses in order to remove a competitor to gasoline. Or it's possible that Cobasys simply wants the market for itself and is waiting for a major automaker to start producing plug-in hybrids or electric vehicles."<sup id="cite_ref-newsociety2007_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-newsociety2007-152">[152]</a></sup>  In an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>, the ECD Ovonics founder Stan Ovshinsky disagreed, stating "Cobasys isn't preventing anything. Cobasys just needs an infusion of cash. They build a great battery"."<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup></p><p>In October 2007, International Acquisitions Services and Innovative Transportation Systems filed suit against Cobasys and its parents for failure to fill an order for large-format NiMH batteries to be used in the electric Innovan.<sup id="cite_ref-ECD_Ovonics_10-Q_Quarterly_Report_154-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECD_Ovonics_10-Q_Quarterly_Report-154">[154]</a></sup>  In August 2008, <a href="/wiki/Mercedes-Benz_U.S._International" title="Mercedes-Benz U.S. International">Mercedes-Benz U.S. International</a> filed suit against Cobasys, on the ground Cobasys did not tender the batteries it agreed to build for Mercedes-Benz's planned hybrid SUV.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> The Mercedes suit was settled for $1.3 million dollars.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Niger_Delta_shootings">Niger Delta shootings</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Niger Delta shootings" data-section="21" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On May 28, 1998, <a href="/wiki/Activist" class="mw-redirect" title="Activist">activists</a> staged a demonstration and took several individuals hostage on a company oil platform in the <a href="/wiki/Niger_Delta" title="Niger Delta">Niger Delta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>. Nigerian police and soldiers were allegedly flown in with Chevron helicopters.<sup id="cite_ref-Democracy_Now!_157-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Democracy_Now!-157">[157]</a></sup> Soldiers shot at the activists and subsequently two activists (Jola Ogungbeje and Aroleka Irowaninu) died from their wounds.<sup id="cite_ref-Democracy_Now!_157-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Democracy_Now!-157">[157]</a></sup>  In 2007 U.S. District Judge <a href="/wiki/Susan_Illston" title="Susan Illston">Susan Illston</a>, allowed a lawsuit brought by victims and victims' families against Chevron to proceed, saying that there may be evidence that Chevron had hired, supervised, and/or provided transportation to Nigerian military forces known for their "general history of committing abuses."<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup> In December 2008, a federal jury cleared Chevron of all charges brought against them in the case.  Chevron had stated that the military intervention was necessary to protect the lives of its workers and considers the jury's decision vindication for the accusations of wrongdoing.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="UN_sanctions">UN sanctions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: UN sanctions" data-section="22" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>According to US Embassy Cable BAGHDAD 000791 the Iraqi prime minister believed that Chevron was engaged in negotiations to invest in Iran in contravention of UN sanctions.  The embassy related that it had no independent confirmation of this claim.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> This document was intended to have been kept secret until 2029.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Richmond.2C_California_refinery"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Richmond,_California_refinery">Richmond, California refinery</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Richmond, California refinery" data-section="23" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chevron_Richmond_Refinery" title="Chevron Richmond Refinery">Richmond refinery</a> paid $540,000 in 1998 for illegally bypassing waste water treatments and failing to notify the public about toxic releases.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> Overall, Chevron is listed as potentially liable for 95 <a href="/wiki/Superfund" title="Superfund">Superfund</a> sites, with funds set aside by the EPA for clean-up.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (March 2015)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup></p><p>A 1989 explosion and fire at the refinery<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> resulted in a $877,000 <a href="/wiki/Occupational_Safety_and_Health_Administration" title="Occupational Safety and Health Administration">OSHA</a> fine for "willfully failing to provide protective equipment for employees." Chevron employees had "repeatedly requested" protective equipment since the early 1980s but the company had refused despite more than 70 fires in the plant since 1984. <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Dole" title="Elizabeth Dole">Elizabeth Dole</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Secretary_of_Labor" title="United States Secretary of Labor">US Secretary of Labor</a>, said: "OSHA's investigation makes clear that Chevron knew of the need for protective equipment and clothing."<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup></p><p>On March 25, 1999, an explosion and fire at the refinery spread noxious fumes and sent hundreds of Richmond residents to hospitals.<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup></p><p>On August 6, 2012, a large fire erupted at the refinery.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bender_168-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bender-168">[168]</a></sup> Initial reports estimated that 11,000 people sought treatment at area hospitals,<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> and later reports placed the number above 15,000 people.<sup id="cite_ref-dn-2013_170-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn-2013-170">[170]</a></sup> The company pleaded no contest to six charges in connection with the fire, and agreed to pay $2 million in fines and restitution.<sup id="cite_ref-guardian-2013_171-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-guardian-2013-171">[171]</a></sup> Around the same time the settlement was announced, the Richmond city council voted to file suit against Chevron. The reasons for the suit included "a continuation of years of neglect, lax oversight and corporate indifference to necessary safety inspection and repairs."<sup id="cite_ref-dn-2013_170-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dn-2013-170">[170]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Oil_spill_off_the_coast_of_Rio_de_Janeiro">Oil spill off the coast of Rio de Janeiro</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Oil spill off the coast of Rio de Janeiro" data-section="24" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_Brazil" title="Energy in Brazil">Energy in Brazil</a></div>
<p>On November 8, 2011, Chevron came under fire by Brazilian authorities for its role in the spill of crude oil off of the southeastern coast of Brazil.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> The Brazilian regulators said 416,400 liters of oil leaked over the course of two weeks from undersea rock near the well in <a href="/wiki/Oil_megaprojects_(2010)" title="Oil megaprojects (2010)">the Frade oil project</a> 370 km off the Brazilian coast.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> Prosecutors in Brazil initially demanded $10.6bn in the subsequent lawsuit. The National Petroleum Agency (ANP) suspended Chevron's activities in Brazil until it identified the cause of an oil spill off the coast of <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup></p><p>The National Petroleum Agency later concluded that the spill did not cause significant economic damage, injured no one, and never approached Brazil's coast.  Criminal charges were dropped and the lawsuits were settled for a total of $130 million.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="KS_Endeavor_explosion"><i>KS Endeavor</i> explosion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: KS Endeavor explosion" data-section="25" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>The <i>KS Endeavor</i> <a href="/wiki/Jackup_rig" title="Jackup rig">jackup rig</a> exploded on January 16, 2012, while drilling an exploration well for Chevron in the Funiwa field in Nigeria.  The explosion resulted in the death of two of the 154 workers on board and a fire that burned for 46 days before the well was sealed on June 18. According to a Reuters news report, workers on the KS Endeavor were ignored by Chevron when they requested evacuation due to concerns of increasing smoke billowing from the drilling borehole.  A senior worker said the blowout was triggered by a massive build-up of pressure.  A witness said that rig engineers advised Chevron to stop drilling and evacuate staff but Chevron told them to continue with drilling. Expecting an explosion, the rig manager, one of the two that later died, kept the lifeboats at hand and ready for use.  A witness reported: "This is the reason so many of us survived because we were all aware that it was going to happen, but just didn't know when."
In an email response to Reuters, Chevron said it did not receive requests to evacuate the rig and that staff on board had the right to call a halt to work if they believed conditions were unsafe.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-upstream170112_178-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-upstream170112-178">[178]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span id="Forest_Fire_in_Lawachara_National_Park.2C_Bangladesh"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Forest_Fire_in_Lawachara_National_Park,_Bangladesh">Forest Fire in Lawachara National Park, Bangladesh</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Forest Fire in Lawachara National Park, Bangladesh" data-section="26" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>On June 26, 2008, a forest fire broke out in Lawachara National Park, Bangladesh, while Chevron was carrying out a 3D seismic survey.  Chevron stated that it was not conducting activities in the area in which the fire broke out.<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">[180]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Polish_gas_exploration">Polish gas exploration</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Polish gas exploration" data-section="27" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>Chevron has experienced protests aimed at the company by local communities in Southern <a href="/wiki/Poland" title="Poland">Poland</a> when they started gas exploration in the region. Their complaint is that Chevron didn't provide all of the documents required for gas exploration in Poland, and that the company has not promised to share a percentage of the revenues with the local landholders. The landholders of the region view Chevron's presence in the region negatively since they may be forced to sell their properties at a low cost if gas is discovered in the region.  As well, potential environmental disasters are a concern for local farmers.  Another of the residents' primary concern is water pollution from the chemicals used in fracking. In response to some of the protests, Chevron has sued some of the protesters from <a href="/wiki/%C5%BBurawl%C3%B3w" title="Żurawlów">Żurawlów</a> for disrupting their operations.<sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">[181]</a></sup></p><p>According to gas and oil expert Andrzej Szczesniak, one of the main reasons for the protest is the difference between Polish and American law. In the USA property owners typically receive 15-20% from the income of gas exploration.  In Poland, the discovery of gas on private property usually results in a forced sale of the property, with the owner receiving only the prior value of the land and no percentage of the gas revenue. This is the result of outdated, Communist Era laws that are still on the books and which are often exploited by municipal governments if they can get a 'kick back' from a larger company.<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Argentina_agreement_and_protests">Argentina agreement and protests</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Argentina agreement and protests" data-section="28" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>After the 2012 decision of the Argentine government to regain control of the biggest oil company of the country, <a href="/wiki/YPF" title="YPF">YPF</a>, the search for foreign investors for exploitation of unconventional oil started. Finally in 2013, YPF and Chevron signed an agreement for the <a href="/wiki/Vaca_Muerta_oil_field" class="mw-redirect" title="Vaca Muerta oil field">Vaca Muerta oil field</a>, the world's second-largest shale gas deposit. In August 2013, the Congress of Neuquén province approved the agreement, while between 5,000<sup id="cite_ref-csmonitor.com_184-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csmonitor.com-184">[184]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">[185]</a></sup> and 10,000<sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">[186]</a></sup> workers, students and indigenous people protested outside the legislature. Police fired rubber bullets, hitting some protesters.<sup id="cite_ref-csmonitor.com_184-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-csmonitor.com-184">[184]</a></sup>  Governor Jorge Sapag defended the police actions: "The march was generally peaceful, but about 100 people separated from the rest and attacked the police. The police acted with seriousness and professionalism."<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Public_Eye_Lifetime_Award">Public Eye Lifetime Award</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Public Eye Lifetime Award" data-section="29" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In 2015, Chevron received the <i>Lifetime Award</i> of the <a href="/wiki/Public_Eye_on_Davos" title="Public Eye on Davos">Public Eye on Davos</a> for what the sponsors called Chevron's responsibility for environmental disaster in the Amazon.<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">[188]</a></sup> The same group cited the company in 2006 in the category "Environment" for oil soiling in the <a href="/wiki/Amazon_Rainforest" class="mw-redirect" title="Amazon Rainforest">Amazonas</a> in Ecuador.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">[189]</a></sup> A Chevron spokesperson commented that the award was "nothing more than a stunt to distract attention from the fact that the lawsuit against Chevron in Ecuador has been proven to be meritless and the product of unprecedented fraud" and pointed to a U.S. court finding that the plaintiff's lawyers had committed "mail and wire fraud, money laundering, witness tampering and obstruction of justice."
<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">[190]</a></sup> That controversial RICO case is under appeal and has been criticized by environmental and human rights groups.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">[191]</a></sup></p>
<h3 class="in-block"><span class="mw-headline" id="Global_warming">Global warming</span><span class="mw-editsection"><a href="/w/index.php?title=Chevron_Corporation&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Global warming" data-section="30" class="mw-ui-icon mw-ui-icon-element mw-ui-icon-wikimedia-edit-base20 edit-page mw-ui-icon-flush-right">Edit</a></span></h3>
<p>In a letter Chevron Corp. argued that under current disclosure rules companies are already required to disclose material risks including climate-change risk, during part of the <a href="/wiki/U.S._Securities_and_Exchange_Commission" title="U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission">U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission</a>'s consultation process, noting that its "2015 <a href="/wiki/Form_10-K" title="Form 10-K">Form 10-K</a> included a significant discussion of the potential risks of additional <a href="/wiki/Greenhouse_gas" title="Greenhouse gas">greenhouse gas</a> emissions <a href="/wiki/Delegated_legislation" class="mw-redirect" title="Delegated legislation">regulation</a> following the outcome of the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Agreement" title="Paris Agreement">Paris Accord</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">[192]</a></sup></p><p>Chevron was found to have contributed 43.35bn tonnes of CO<sub>2</sub> equivalent since 1965 in an analysis made by the Climate Accountability Institute.<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">[193]</a></sup></p>

<li id="cite_note-dn-2013-170"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-dn-2013_170-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-dn-2013_170-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.democracynow.org/2013/8/6/chevron_to_pay_2_million_for">"Chevron to Pay $2 Million for 2012 Refinery Fire in Richmond, CA; 200 Arrested at Protest"</a>. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">August 6,</span> 2013</span>. <q>It was one year ago when a massive fire at a Chevron refinery in Richmond, California, sent toxic smoke billowing into the air about 10 miles northeast of San Francisco. In the aftermath, more than 15,000 people sought medical treatment for respiratory problems. On Monday, Chevron pleaded no contest to six criminal charges related to the fire and agreed to submit to additional oversight over the next few years and pay $2 million in fines and restitution as part of a plea deal with state and county prosecutors. Two days earlier, thousands of people marched to condemn safety issues at Chevron's plant and to call for renewable alternatives to fossil fuels.</q></cite><span title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=unknown&amp;rft.btitle=Chevron+to+Pay+%242+Million+for+2012+Refinery+Fire+in+Richmond%2C+CA%3B+200+Arrested+at+Protest&amp;rft.pub=Democracy+Now%21&amp;rft.date=2013-08-06&amp;rft_id=http%3A%2F%2Fwww.democracynow.org%2F2013%2F8%2F6%2Fchevron_to_pay_2_million_for&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AChevron+Corporation" class="Z3988"></span><link rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style" href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r935243608"></span>
